08/05/2022 20:15:13None, NonewanderlustiggelinkThis is a Bear cache, it is effective at keeping animals away from meat that had been freshly killed. Customary of the ancient traditions of the Athabascan people, the boxes often resembled small wooden cabins on stilts. In a pinch, a tree would be used to support the bear box. The box would encircle the tree, and the tree would act as a support . ¬†Places that have a high amount of predatory or scavenging animals tend to have a history of people using similar containers. The traditional look for Alaska bear caches is a simple design using a¬†box structure that is raised on four tall legs. The legs are spread apart from each other and at an angle that makes it difficult for tenacious bears (and other animals) to reach the food stored in the box. Boxes would typically open from the front, but it wasn‚Äôt unheard of to see them accessible from the bottom. that would In Alaska, the main intent of the bear cache was to keep food away from bears and other animals who might be looking for an easy meal. People would employ bear caches to keep perishable and non-perishable goods safe from animals.¬† #bearcache #alaskanativeheritagecenter #alaska #foodstorage #nativepeople #athabasca #athabascanpeople #nativeamericanheritage #nativepride #educationiskeylink

05/17/2022 22:24:5761.1765085461, -149.8458416023motocannlink1968 Triumph 650cc TR6R Trophy: 1968 was a transitional year for the British motorcycle. Engine upgrades, an exhaust cam was replaced with a more radical E3134 racing cam, making both the intake & exhaust the same, which it now had in common with the Bonneville. 1-1/8-inch cam followers continued to be specified for both inlet & exhaust. The ‚ÄòRed Dot‚Äô outer valve springs were replaced by ‚ÄòGreen Dot‚Äô springs with 10% more load when fully open, but retaining the original loading when closed. Starting with Engine #DU81209 the internal oilways in the rocker arms were deleted, adding strength to cope with the stronger springs. Stronger connecting rods with a greater cross-section & the H&G pistons were redesigned (removing the bar under the crown & thickening the ring groove-area. Left-hand threads were specified for the tachometer (rev counter) drive. To make more room for wrenches (spanners) the cylinder base nuts were changed to 12-points. TIMING IS EVERYTHING For the 1968 Triumph TR6, there were 3 different ignition timing regimens indicated on the crankcase & flywheel providing TDC (Top Dead Center) & 38-degrees BTDC (Before Top Dead Center GEARBOX STUFF Lots of internal changes were made to the gearbox including the mainshaft high gear, oil seals, clutch operating mechanism & the whole thing was converted over to UNF threads. The 1968 Triumph TR6 got a new primary cover with a round removable inspection plate over the rotor to aid ignition timing. And staring with Engine #DU85346 a pointer was added to the crankcase to aid in the process. BIG NEWS: NEW TLS FRONT BRAKE The 1968 Triumph TR6 received an all-new 8-inch TLS (Twin Leading Shoe) front brake, arguably the best Triumph Motodycles ever put on a classic Triumph. The dalton highway was created in 1974 and provides the only road that connects the trans-Atlantic pipeline to the rest of the world. It‚Äôs considered the loneliest road in America because it is the most isolated and least traveled. This highway is banned by most rental car companies (oops) and has claimed the lives of dozens of people. 08/25/2022 18:10:1064.85849493, -147.84228193historycoolkidsHistory Cool KidslinkBlue Babe is a 50,000 year old mummified steppe bison that was discovered by gold miners in 1979, north of Fairbanks, Alaska. Claw and tooth marks on the rear of the bison indicate that it was killed by a North American lion, an extinct Ice Age cat that was 25% larger than the modern lion. The lion managed to open the bison carcass and eat most of its muscle located in the ribs and upper limbs area. However, the bison carcass froze quickly, making it difficult for scavengers to fully consume. In 1984, a group of paleontologists decided to cook and eat part of the neck muscle of the bison carcass. Professor emeritus of zoology at the University of Alaska, R Dale Guthrie, wrote about the event: ‚ÄúTo climax and celebrate [taxidermist] Eirik Granqvist‚Äôs work with Blue Babe, we had a bison stew dinner for him and for Bjorn Kurten ‚Ä¶ A small part of the mummy‚Äôs neck was diced and simmered in a pot of stock and vegetables. We had Blue Babe for dinner. The meat was well aged but still a little tough, and it gave the stew a strong Pleistocene aroma, but nobody there would have dared miss it. The meat in its abdomen had spoiled before the bison was completely frozen. But in the neck area small pieces of meat were found attached to the skull. The lions had left so little there that it had frozen through while the meat was still fresh. When it thawed it gave off an unmistakable beef aroma, not unpleasantly mixed with a faint smell of the earth in which it was found, with a touch of mushroom. About a dozen of us gathered .... on April 6, 1984, to partake of Bison priscus stew. The taste was delicious, and none of us suffered any ill effects from the meal.‚Äù Source:¬†‚ÄúFood History Almanac: Over 1,300 Years of World Culinary History, Culture, and Social Influence‚Äù by Janet Clarksonlink

A few fun facts not in any order: - 2 passenger coach cars (normally 3), 1 baggage car, 170 passengers, 2 locomotives on front and 1 on back. - Total duration , 8:35 duration, top speed in winter: 35mph (faster at up to 50 mph in Summer) for 235 miles. - Flagship route between Fairbanks and Anchorage takes 12 hours at average speed of 30 mph during winter for 350 miles. - Cars built in 1989, customized for Alaskan conditions. 09/02/2021 19:35:4661.162985, -149.69367willowridgeconstructionWillowRidge ConstructionlinkShou Sugi Ban: An ancient Japanese architectural technique that is used to preserve wood by charring the surface with a hot flame. Traditionally performed on Cedar(Sugi) wood. This is a popular application for modern homes not only for its aesthetics, but for its long lasting durability. A few fun facts not in any order: - 2 passenger coach cars (normally 3), 1 baggage car, 170 passengers, 2 locomotives on front and 1 on back. - Total duration , 8:35 duration, top speed in winter: 35mph (faster at up to 50 mph in Summer) for 235 miles. - Flagship route between Fairbanks and Anchorage takes 12 hours at average speed of 30 mph during winter for 350 miles. - Cars built in 1989, customized for Alaskan conditions. These older coaches are more adept for cold conditions. Glass window dual level coaches are difficult to keep warm. - One baggage coach and two dining coaches. - Two locomotive provide pull and redundancy but the train has broken down before. - Emergency food, rations, and blankets are loaded but with generators located on multiple cars, this hasn‚Äôt been cracked. - Load factors today at 100 percent. As low as 20 people for entire train during shoulder seasons and dark winter Jan-Feb - Acquired from the Federal Govt‚Äôt and owned by the State of Alaska. - Operates profitably with no taxpayer money. - Freight service is true cash cow. - What excites passengers the most: seeing a moose - Company owns a number of rail barges with 8 tracks apiece for shipping rail cars from Seattle to railroads‚Äô southern terminus (along with Seward) - Will operate most conditions down to -20 degrees. Issue isn‚Äôt safety but keeping coaches warm. - WiFi and phone service very spotty along the way but who cares? They have had as many as 50 stops in a single trip. 10/07/2021 22:29:3460.7897, -161.779scienceontheflyScience on the FlylinkWe also want to study the Alaskan rivers while we aren‚Äôt on them. We do this with water temperature data loggers. These loggers are hammered into locations that are a good representation of the watershed, accessible for continual retrieval, and out of the way of potential large hydrological and geological events. These data loggers record water temperature and water pressure every hour. We have these loggers placed in both the Kwethluk and Kisaralik rivers. On the Kwethluk River, we installed three water temperature loggers and five soil temperature data loggers (for permafrost) in 2019. The plan was to retrieve them in 2020, but that got pushed back to 2021. This year, a group of three SOTF members went to retrieve those data loggers, upload the data from the sensor, and continue collecting water samples along the river. This group was able to successfully retrieve 1 out of the 3 river logger closer towards the headwaters of the Kwethluk and none of the permafrost loggers. The fact that we got one temperature logger was a success. These rivers can change fairly rapidly, and the Kwethluk River seems to be one of the worst. We believe we didn‚Äôt located all the sensors due to an increase in sedimentation which would bury it (sometimes under a couple of feet mud) or the braided channels changed enough to bury or displace it. Our favorite reason- a fox took the permafrost logger. We were able to find the cable, it had just been chewed to pieces. The logger that we did successfully retrieve gave us about two year‚Äôs worth of temperature data that you can see on the graph. On The Kisaralik River we placed three water temperature loggers. One was placed right below the lake. One was placed on day four just before the braids started, and the last was placed in a small tributary. The logger that we placed in the small tributary was the hotspot for Arctic Grayling dry fly fishing. The grayling were flashing their beautiful dorsal fin out of the water and eating each of our dry flies. Each one prettier than the last. We‚Äôre excited to go back and check on that water temperature logger and the grayling. üìà: @lindobaggins üì∏: @johnlandlecoq @srockwoodlink

The start of the season brings some of the earliest-departing species preparing to embark on their journey south. Alder Flycatchers are the most fleeting of all: the last species to arrive in the spring (early June), they typically are already leaving their breeding grounds by the end of July.
